/>.com</a></span></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Virgin Atlantic</b>, a <a href="/wiki/Trade_name" title="Trade name">trading name</a> of <b>Virgin Atlantic Airways Limited</b> and <b>Virgin Atlantic International Limited</b>, is a <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">British</a> <a href="/wiki/Airline" title="Airline">airline</a> with its head office in <a href="/wiki/Crawley" title="Crawley">Crawley</a>, England. The airline was established in 1984 as <i>British Atlantic Airways</i>, and was originally planned by its co-founders <a href="/wiki/Randolph_Fields" title="Randolph Fields">Randolph Fields</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alan_Hellary" title="Alan Hellary">Alan Hellary</a> to fly between <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Falkland_Islands" title="Falkland Islands">Falkland Islands</a>. Soon after changing the name to Virgin Atlantic Airways, Fields sold his shares in the company after disagreements with Sir <a href="/wiki/Richard_Branson" title="Richard Branson">Richard Branson</a> over the management of the company. The maiden flight from <a href="/wiki/Gatwick_Airport" title="Gatwick Airport">Gatwick Airport</a> to <a href="/wiki/Newark_Liberty_International_Airport" title="Newark Liberty International Airport">Newark Liberty International Airport</a> took place on 22 June 1984.\n</p><p>The airline along with <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Holidays" title="Virgin Holidays">Virgin Holidays</a> is controlled by a holding company, Virgin Atlantic Limited, which is 51% owned by the <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Group" title="Virgin Group">Virgin Group</a> and 49% by <a href="/wiki/Delta_Air_Lines" title="Delta Air Lines">Delta Air Lines</a>. It is administratively separate from other Virgin-branded airlines. Virgin Atlantic Airways Limited and Virgin Atlantic International Limited both hold <a href="/wiki/Civil_Aviation_Authority_(United_Kingdom)" title="Civil Aviation Authority (United Kingdom)">Civil Aviation Authority</a> (CAA) Type A Operating Licences (<a href="/wiki/Air_operator%27s_certificate" title="Air operator&#39;s certificate">AOC</a> numbers 534<sup id="cite_ref-AOC_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AOC-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> and 2435 respectively),<sup id="cite_ref-AOC_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AOC-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> both of which permit these airlines, operating as Virgin Atlantic Airways, to carry passengers, cargo and mail on aircraft with 20 or more seats.<sup id="cite_ref-Licence_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Licence-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Virgin Atlantic uses a mixed fleet of <a href="/wiki/Airbus" title="Airbus">Airbus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Boeing_Commercial_Airplanes" title="Boeing Commercial Airplanes">Boeing</a> <a href="/wiki/Wide-body_aircraft" title="Wide-body aircraft">wide-body aircraft</a> and operates to destinations in North America, the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a>, Africa, the Middle East and Asia from its main base at <a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Airport" title="Heathrow Airport">Heathrow</a>, and its secondary base at <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Airport" title="Manchester Airport">Manchester</a>. The airline also operates seasonal flights from <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Airport" title="Glasgow Airport">Glasgow</a> and <a href="/wiki/Belfast_International_Airport" title="Belfast International Airport">Belfast</a>. Virgin Atlantic aircraft consist of three cabins: Economy, Premium (formerly <a href="/wiki/Premium_economy" class="mw-redirect" title="Premium economy">Premium economy</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-:0_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> and Upper Class (business).\n</p><p>In July 2017, Virgin Atlantic announced its intention to form a joint venture with <a href="/wiki/Air_France%E2%80%93KLM" title="Air France\xe2\x80\x93KLM">Air France\xe2\x80\x93KLM</a>, but in December 2019, it was announced that the joint venture would not include a stake in the company.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 5 May 2020, it was announced that due to the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a>, the airline would be laying off 3000 staff, reducing the fleet size to 35 by the summer of 2022, retiring the <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747-400" title="Boeing 747-400">Boeing 747-400s</a><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> and would not be resuming operations from Gatwick following the pandemic.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Virgin Atlantic filed for Chapter 15 Bankruptcy Protection in New York on 4 August 2020 as part of a \xc2\xa31.2 billion private refinancing package.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" tocsection-19"><a href="#Destinations"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">Destinations</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-20"><a href="#Codeshare_agreements"><span class="tocnumber">3.1</span> <span class="toctext">Codeshare agreements</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-21"><a href="#Fleet"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Fleet</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-22"><a href="#Current_fleet"><span class="tocnumber">4.1</span> <span class="toctext">Current fleet</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-23"><a href="#Fleet_development"><span class="tocnumber">4.2</span> <span class="toctext">Fleet development</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-24"><a href="#Historical_fleet"><span class="tocnumber">4.3</span> <span class="toctext">Historical fleet</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-25"><a href="#Livery"><span class="tocnumber">4.4</span> <span class="toctext">Livery</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-26"><a href="#Incidents_and_accidents"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Incidents and accidents</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-27"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-28"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-29"><a href="#Citations"><span class="tocnumber">7.1</span> <span class="toctext">Citations</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-30"><a href="#Bibliography"><span class="tocnumber">7.2</span> <span class="toctext">Bibliography</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-31"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Virgin_Atlantic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Origins">Origins</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Virgin_Atlantic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Origins">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Virgin_Atlantic_launch_press_conference.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Virgin_Atlantic_launch_press_conference.png/220px-Virgin_Atlantic_launch_press_conference.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Virgin_Atlantic_launch_press_conference.png/330px-Virgin_Atlantic_launch_press_conference.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/f/f3/Virgin_Atlantic_launch_press_conference.png 2x" data-file-width="388" data-file-height="257" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Virgin_Atlantic_launch_press_conference.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Alan_Hellary" title="Alan Hellary">Alan Hellary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Richard_Branson" title="Richard Branson">Richard Branson</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Randolph_Fields" title="Randolph Fields">Randolph Fields</a> launch Virgin Atlantic at the 1984 press conference</div></div></div>\n<p>Virgin Atlantic has its origins in a joint endeavour by <a href="/wiki/Randolph_Fields" title="Randolph Fields">Randolph Fields</a>, an American-born lawyer, and <a href="/wiki/Alan_Hellary" title="Alan Hellary">Alan Hellary</a>, a former chief pilot for British private airline <a href="/wiki/Laker_Airways" title="Laker Airways">Laker Airways</a>. Following the collapse of Laker Airways in 1982, Field and Hellary decided to establish a new company, initially named <i>British Atlantic Airways</i>, as a successor.<sup id="cite_ref-Virgin_Birth_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Virgin_Birth-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> Reportedly, Fields had formed a concept for an airline that would operate between London and the <a href="/wiki/Falkland_Islands" title="Falkland Islands">Falkland Islands</a> during June 1982, when the <a href="/wiki/Falklands_War" title="Falklands War">Falklands War</a> had just finished.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Seeking out expertise in the field, Fields made contact with Hellary, who had already been considering options for establishing a regular commercial service to the Falklands. In turn, Hellary was in contact with several out-of-colleagues from the collapse of Laker Airways; as such, the pair decided to refine their ambitions.\n</p><p>However, it was soon determined that the short runway at <a href="/wiki/Port_Stanley_Airport" title="Port Stanley Airport">Port Stanley Airport</a>, and the time it would take to improve it, would render a route to the Falklands commercially unviable, thus the idea of such a service was dropped. In its place, Hellary and Fields commenced efforts to secure a licence to operate a route <a href="/wiki/Gatwick_Airport" title="Gatwick Airport">Gatwick Airport</a>, <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport" title="John F. Kennedy International Airport">John F. Kennedy International Airport</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>. During May 1983, a three-day inquiry was conducted, which chose to reject the application following objections from <a href="/wiki/British_Airways" title="British Airways">British Airways</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_Caledonian" title="British Caledonian">British Caledonian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Airport_Holdings" title="Heathrow Airport Holdings">BAA</a>.\n</p><p>Hellary and Fields then applied for a licence between Gatwick and <a href="/wiki/Newark_Liberty_International_Airport" title="Newark Liberty International Airport">Newark</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey" title="New Jersey">New Jersey</a>, using a 380-seat <a href="/wiki/McDonnell_Douglas_DC-10" title="McDonnell Douglas DC-10">McDonnell Douglas DC-10</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Virgin_Birth_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Virgin_Birth-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> However, faced with the prospect of direct competition from rival operator <a href="/wiki/People_Express_Airlines_(1980s)" title="People Express Airlines (1980s)">PEOPLExpress</a>, a post-<a href="/wiki/Deregulation" title="Deregulation">deregulation</a> "no frills" discount airline based at Newark, they decided to secure more funding before proceeding. Fields met British entrepreneur <a href="/wiki/Richard_Branson" title="Richard Branson">Richard Branson</a> at a party in London during which he proposed a business partnership. After protracted and testy negotiations, Fields agreed to a reduced stake of 25% in the airline (which was renamed <i>Virgin Atlantic</i>) and became its first chairman. Following disagreements over operations, Fields agreed to be bought out for an initial sum of \xc2\xa31&#160;million with further payment on Virgin Atlantic\'s first dividend. As a result of a <a href="/wiki/High_Court_of_Justice" title="High Court of Justice">High Court</a> action, this additional payment was received shortly before Fields\' death in 1997.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Formative_years">Formative years</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Virgin_Atlantic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Formative years">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Virgin_Atlantic_G-VIRG_by_Steve_Fitzgerald.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Virgin_Atlantic_G-VIRG_by_Steve_Fitzgerald.jpg/220px-Virgin_Atlantic_G-VIRG_by_Steve_Fitzgerald.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Virgin_Atlantic_G-VIRG_by_Steve_Fitzgerald.jpg/330px-Virgin_Atlantic_G-VIRG_by_Steve_Fitzgerald.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Virgin_Atlantic_G-VIRG_by_Steve_Fitzgerald.jpg/440px-Virgin_Atlantic_G-VIRG_by_Steve_Fitzgerald.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="683" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Virgin_Atlantic_G-VIRG_by_Steve_Fitzgerald.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Boeing_747-200" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 747-200">Boeing 747-200</a> <i>Maiden Voyager</i> operated the first scheduled Virgin Atlantic service on 22 June 1984</div></div></div>\n<p>On 22 June 1984, Virgin Atlantic operated its inaugural scheduled service, flown between Gatwick and Newark using a leased <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747-200" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 747-200">Boeing 747-200</a> (registration <span class="nowrap">G-VIRG</span>), christened <i>Maiden Voyager</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-Virgin_Birth_14-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Virgin_Birth-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> which had been formerly operated by <a href="/wiki/Aerol%C3%ADneas_Argentinas" title="Aerol\xc3\xadneas Argentinas">Aerol\xc3\xadneas Argentinas</a>. From the onset, its activities were augmented by leveraging existing <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Group" title="Virgin Group">Virgin Group</a> resources, such as tickets being sold at <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Megastores" title="Virgin Megastores">Virgin Megastores</a> record shops.<sup id="cite_ref-hilo_09_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hilo_09-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Part of Richard Branson\'s declared approach to business is to either succeed within the first year or exit the market; this ethos includes a one-year limit being expressed upon everything associated with starting up operations.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Virgin Atlantic became profitable within the first 12 months, aided by sister company <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Records" title="Virgin Records">Virgin Records</a>\' ability to finance the <a href="/wiki/Aircraft_lease" title="Aircraft lease">lease</a> of a secondhand Boeing&#160;747. The firm had timed its operations to take advantage of a full summer, from June to September, which was typically the most profitable period of the year.\n</p><p>In November 1984 the airline launched a service between Gatwick Airport and <a href="/wiki/Maastricht_Aachen_Airport" title="Maastricht Aachen Airport">Maastricht Aachen Airport</a> in the Netherlands using a chartered <a href="/wiki/BAC_One-Eleven" title="BAC One-Eleven">BAC One-Eleven</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1986 the airline added another Boeing&#160;747 to its fleet and started a scheduled route from Gatwick to <a href="/wiki/Miami_International_Airport" title="Miami International Airport">Miami</a>. Additional aircraft were quickly acquired and new routes launched from Gatwick, such as to <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport" title="John F. Kennedy International Airport">New York JFK</a> in 1988, <a href="/wiki/Narita_International_Airport" title="Narita International Airport">Tokyo Narita</a> in 1989, <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_International_Airport" title="Los Angeles International Airport">Los Angeles</a> in 1990, <a href="/wiki/Logan_International_Airport" title="Logan International Airport">Boston</a> in 1991, and <a href="/wiki/Orlando_International_Airport" title="Orlando International Airport">Orlando</a> in 1992. In 1987, Virgin Atlantic launched a service between <a href="/wiki/London_Luton_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="London Luton Airport">Luton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dublin_Airport" title="Dublin Airport">Dublin</a> using secondhand <a href="/wiki/Vickers_Viscount" title="Vickers Viscount">Vickers Viscount</a> <a href="/wiki/Turboprop" title="Turboprop">turboprop</a> aircraft, but this route was withdrawn around 1990. The airline was also operating Viscount service between Maastricht and London Luton Airport in 1989.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>  During 1988, <a href="/wiki/Club_Air" title="Club Air">Club Air</a> operated two <a href="/wiki/Boeing_727" title="Boeing 727">Boeing&#160;727</a> <a href="/wiki/Jet_aircraft" title="Jet aircraft">jet aircraft</a> on behalf of Virgin Atlantic; these served the Luton to Dublin route until about 1990.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Competition">Competition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Virgin_Atlantic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Competition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="box-Cite_check plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Text_document_with_red_question_mark.svg" class="image"><img alt="Text document with red question mark.svg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Text_document_with_red_question_mark.svg/60px-Text_document_with_red_question_mark.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Text_document_with_red_question_mark.svg/80px-Text_document_with_red_question_mark.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="48" data-file-height="48" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>possibly contains inappropriate or misinterpreted <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:CITE" class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/File:Airbus_A340-311,_Virgin_Atlantic_Airways_AN0062857.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Airbus_A340-311%2C_Virgin_Atlantic_Airways_AN0062857.jpg/220px-Airbus_A340-311%2C_Virgin_Atlantic_Airways_AN0062857.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="131" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Airbus_A340-311%2C_Virgin_Atlantic_Airways_AN0062857.jpg/330px-Airbus_A340-311%2C_Virgin_Atlantic_Airways_AN0062857.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Airbus_A340-311%2C_Virgin_Atlantic_Airways_AN0062857.jpg/440px-Airbus_A340-311%2C_Virgin_Atlantic_Airways_AN0062857.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="476" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Airbus_A340-311,_Virgin_Atlantic_Airways_AN0062857.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Airbus_A340#A340-300" title="Airbus A340">Airbus A340-300</a> landing at <a href="/wiki/Kai_Tak_Airport" title="Kai Tak Airport">Kai Tak Airport</a>, displaying the "No Way BA/AA" sticker</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Virgin_Atlantic_A340-300_G-VHOL_LHR_2003-6-12.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Virgin_Atlantic_A340-300_G-VHOL_LHR_2003-6-12.png/220px-Virgin_Atlantic_A340-300_G-VHOL_LHR_2003-6-12.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Virgin_Atlantic_A340-300_G-VHOL_LHR_2003-6-12.png/330px-Virgin_Atlantic_A340-300_G-VHOL_LHR_2003-6-12.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Virgin_Atlantic_A340-300_G-VHOL_LHR_2003-6-12.png/440px-Virgin_Atlantic_A340-300_G-VHOL_LHR_2003-6-12.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="790" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Virgin_Atlantic_A340-300_G-VHOL_LHR_2003-6-12.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Airbus_A340#A340-300" title="Airbus A340">Airbus A340-300</a> at <a href="/wiki/London_Heathrow_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="London Heathrow Airport">London Heathrow Airport</a> in 2003, displaying "4 Engines 4 Longhaul" slogan</div></div></div>\n<p>Before Virgin Atlantic started operations, British Airways had been the only airline from the United Kingdom serving long-haul routes to destinations in North America, the Caribbean, and the Far East since the <a href="/wiki/British_Caledonian_in_the_1980s#British_Airways_wins_the_day" title="British Caledonian in the 1980s">BA-BCal merger</a> in the late 1980s. In 1991, Virgin Atlantic was given permission to operate from Heathrow following the abolition of the London Air Traffic Distribution Rules (TDRs), which had governed the distribution of traffic between Heathrow and Gatwick airports since 1978, primarily to bolster the profitability of Gatwick. Airlines without an international scheduled service from Heathrow prior to 1 April 1977 were obliged to operate from Gatwick. However, airlines that did not already operate at Heathrow were still able to begin domestic scheduled services there provided BAA, which then ran both Heathrow and Gatwick on behalf of the UK government, and the <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_for_Transport" title="Secretary of State for Transport">Secretary of State for Transport</a> granted permission.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Civil_Aviation_Authority_(United_Kingdom)" title="Civil Aviation Authority (United Kingdom)">Civil Aviation Authority</a> also transferred two pairs of unused <a href="/wiki/Landing_slot" title="Landing slot">landing slots</a> that British Airways held at Tokyo\'s <a href="/wiki/Narita_International_Airport" title="Narita International Airport">Narita Airport</a> to Virgin Atlantic; allowing it to increase frequency between Heathrow and Tokyo from four to six weekly round trips, making it easier to compete against British Airways. The then-chairman of BA <a href="/wiki/John_King,_Baron_King_of_Wartnaby" title="John King, Baron King of Wartnaby">Lord King</a> called the CAA\'s decision, which the government had endorsed, "a confiscation of his company\'s property".<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the year to October 1993, Virgin Atlantic declared a loss of \xc2\xa39.3m. The decision to abolish the London TDRs and to let Virgin Atlantic operate at Heathrow, in competition with British Airways, became the trigger for BA\'s so-called <a href="/wiki/Dirty_Tricks_(British_Airways_scandal)" class="mw-redirect" title="Dirty Tricks (British Airways scandal)">"dirty tricks" campaign</a> against the company. During 1993, BA\'s <a href="/wiki/Public_relations" title="Public relations">public relations</a> director, <a href="/wiki/David_Burnside" title="David Burnside">David Burnside</a>, published an article in <i>BA News</i>, British Airways\' internal magazine, which argued that Branson\'s protests against British Airways were a publicity stunt. Branson sued British Airways for libel, using the services of <a href="/wiki/George_Carman" title="George Carman">George Carman</a> <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_Counsel" title="Queen&#39;s Counsel">QC</a>. BA settled out of court when its lawyers discovered the lengths to which the company had gone in trying to kill off Virgin Atlantic. British Airways had to pay a legal bill of up to \xc2\xa33&#160;million, damages to Branson of \xc2\xa3500,000, and a further \xc2\xa3110,000 to his airline. Branson reportedly donated the proceeds from the case to Virgin Atlantic staff.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During the 1990s, Virgin Atlantic jets were painted with "No Way BA/AA" as a declaration of its opposition to the attempted merger between British Airways and <a href="/wiki/American_Airlines" title="American Airlines">American Airlines</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> In 1997, following British Airways\' announcement that it was to remove the <a href="/wiki/Union_Flag" class="mw-redirect" title="Union Flag">Union Flag</a> from its tailfins in favour of <a href="/wiki/British_Airways_ethnic_liveries" title="British Airways ethnic liveries">world images</a>, Virgin Atlantic introduced a Union Flag design on the <a href="/wiki/Wingtip_device#Winglet" title="Wingtip device">winglets</a> of its aircraft and changed the red dress on the <i>Scarlet Lady</i> on the nose of aircraft to the union flag with the tag line "Britain\'s <a href="/wiki/Flag_Carrier" class="mw-redirect" title="Flag Carrier">Flag Carrier</a>". This was a tongue-in-cheek challenge to BA\'s traditional role as the UK\'s flag carrier.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In June 2006, US and UK competition authorities investigated alleged <a href="/wiki/Price_fixing" title="Price fixing">price fixing</a> between Virgin Atlantic and British Airways over passenger fuel surcharges.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> In August 2007, BA was fined \xc2\xa3271&#160;million by the UK <a href="/wiki/Office_of_Fair_Trading" title="Office of Fair Trading">Office of Fair Trading</a> (OFT) and the US&#160;<a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Justice" title="United States Department of Justice">Department of Justice</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> However, the Chief Executive of Virgin Atlantic, Steve Ridgway, was forced to admit that the company had been a party to the agreement, had been aware of the price-fixing and had taken no steps whatsoever to stop the price-fixing.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> The company escaped a similar fine to that levied on British Airways only by virtue of the immunity it had earlier negotiated with the regulators.\n</p><p>In April 2010, a tip-off from <a href="/wiki/Cathay_Pacific" title="Cathay Pacific">Cathay Pacific</a> led to the <a href="/wiki/Office_of_Fair_Trading" title="Office of Fair Trading">Office of Fair Trading</a> (OFT) investigating alleged price-fixing between Virgin Atlantic and <a href="/wiki/Cathay_Pacific" title="Cathay Pacific">Cathay Pacific</a> on flights to Hong Kong between 2002 and 2006. Cathay Pacific received immunity from prosecution for reporting the alleged offence. A maximum fine, if found guilty, was 10% of turnover which based on the \xc2\xa32.5&#160;billion in sales for the year to February 2009 would have been \xc2\xa3250&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> At the time, the OFT stressed that it should not be assumed that the parties involved had broken the law.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> The OFT cleared both airlines in December 2012, concluding there were "no grounds for action".<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Recent_years">Recent years</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Virgin_Atlantic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Recent years">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Two_Virgin_Atlantic_Airbus_A340-600.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Two_Virgin_Atlantic_Airbus_A340-600.jpg/220px-Two_Virgin_Atlantic_Airbus_A340-600.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Two_Virgin_Atlantic_Airbus_A340-600.jpg/330px-Two_Virgin_Atlantic_Airbus_A340-600.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Two_Virgin_Atlantic_Airbus_A340-600.jpg/440px-Two_Virgin_Atlantic_Airbus_A340-600.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="849" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Two_Virgin_Atlantic_Airbus_A340-600.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Two Virgin Atlantic <a href="/wiki/A340-600" class="mw-redirect" title="A340-600">A340-600s</a> at London Heathrow</div></div></div>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2014">2014</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Virgin_Atlantic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 2014">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>In May 2014 Virgin Atlantic ended flights to Sydney.\n</p><p>In September 2014 Virgin Atlantic announced plans to scrap flights to Tokyo, Mumbai, Vancouver, and Cape Town, and to <a href="/wiki/Codesharing" class="mw-redirect" title="Codesharing">codeshare</a> transatlantic flights with <a href="/wiki/Delta_Air_Lines" title="Delta Air Lines">Delta Air Lines</a>; the company was also reported to be considering axing its new Little Red domestic airline after suffering heavy losses.<sup id="cite_ref-telegraph_little_red_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-telegraph_little_red-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 6 October 2014, Virgin Atlantic confirmed that Little Red services between London and Manchester would end in March 2015, and that the Scottish routes would be terminated in September 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> Passengers used the routes from point to point as opposed to using it as a connection for longer haul Virgin Atlantic flights. The former BMI routes continued with rival airline British Airways.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2015">2015</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Virgin_Atlantic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 2015">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>In June 2015, Richard Branson admitted that Virgin Atlantic would be in "real trouble" without strategic support from <a href="/wiki/Delta_Air_Lines" title="Delta Air Lines">Delta Air Lines</a>. With cumulative losses between 2010 and 2013 amounting to \xc2\xa3233 million, the future of the 30-year-old airline was in doubt.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> In the same month, the airline announced it would cut 500 jobs to establish a more efficient management structure.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2017">2017</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Virgin_Atlantic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 2017">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>In July 2017, Virgin Atlantic announced its intention to form a joint venture with Air France-KLM. Under the agreement, Air France-KLM would acquire a 31% stake in Virgin Atlantic currently held by Virgin Group for \xc2\xa3220 million, subject to execution of definitive agreements and receipt of the final shareholder, board, and regulatory approvals. Virgin Atlantic would retain its independence as a UK airline with a UK operating certificate, and would continue to fly under the Virgin Atlantic brand.<sup id="cite_ref-partnership_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-partnership-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BBC_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2019">2019</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Virgin_Atlantic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: 2019">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>In 2019, Virgin Atlantic began to allow its female <a href="/wiki/Flight_attendants" class="mw-redirect" title="Flight attendants">flight attendants</a> to not wear makeup and have a choice to wear trousers rather than a skirt.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In September 2019, it was announced Virgin Atlantic had outlined plans for an expansion of its network to create a "second flag carrier" in the UK, should slot reforms being considered for larger Heathrow airport work in its favour. The airline would seek to serve 103 destinations \xe2\x80\x93 comprising domestic, European, and long-haul services \xe2\x80\x93 up from the 19 points it planned to serve in 2020, all of which are long-haul. Of the 84 new destinations planned, 12 are domestic, 37 are European and 35 are international. The 35 new international destinations include <a href="/wiki/Addis_Ababa" title="Addis Ababa">Addis Ababa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Austin" class="mw-redirect" title="Austin">Austin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beijing" title="Beijing">Beijing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bogot%C3%A1" title="Bogot\xc3\xa1">Bogot\xc3\xa1</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buenos_Aires" title="Buenos Aires">Buenos Aires</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cape_Town" title="Cape Town">Cape Town</a>, <a href="/wiki/Karachi" title="Karachi">Karachi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mexico_City" title="Mexico City">Mexico City</a>, <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sydney" title="Sydney">Sydney</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tokyo" title="Tokyo">Tokyo</a>. Most of the routes would be new to Virgin Atlantic, although it has served several of the long-haul destinations \xe2\x80\x93 such as Cape Town, Karachi, Sydney, Tokyo, and Vancouver \xe2\x80\x93 in the past.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> It was confirmed that <a href="/wiki/Flybe" title="Flybe">Flybe</a> would have been a key part of Virgin Atlantic\'s plans for domestic and intra-European services, which involved the rebranding of Flybe as "Virgin Connect" from early 2020, however, the plans fell through when Flybe filed for administration and ceased operations in March 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Flybecollapse_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Flybecollapse-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In December 2019, Branson announced that he would be scrapping the sale of a 31% stake in the airline to Air France-KLM and that Virgin Group would retain its 51% shareholding.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2020">2020</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Virgin_Atlantic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: 2020">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>In March 2020, during the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a>, Richard Branson and Virgin Atlantic attracted criticism by asking employees to take eight weeks\' unpaid leave, however this was before the UK Government announced the <a href="/wiki/British_government_response_to_the_COVID-19_pandemic#Furlough_and_jobs_protection" title="British government response to the COVID-19 pandemic">Coronavirus Job Retention Scheme</a> and subsequently, employees were furloughed instead.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> Whilst furloughed many staff volunteered with the NHS answering 999 calls and at NHS Trusts in London and the South East.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 27 March it was reported that Virgin Atlantic was expected to be seeking a government bailout, which was on 1 April reportedly backed by <a href="/wiki/Rolls-Royce_Holdings" title="Rolls-Royce Holdings">Rolls Royce</a>, <a href="/wiki/Airbus" title="Airbus">Airbus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Airport" title="Heathrow Airport">Heathrow</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In May 2020 Virgin Atlantic announced more than 3,000 jobs losses in the UK and that they were to end operations at <a href="/wiki/Gatwick_Airport" title="Gatwick Airport">Gatwick Airport</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In July 2020 Virgin Atlantic announced it had secured funding to survive for another 18 months.\n</p><p>On 4 August Virgin Atlantic filed for <a href="/wiki/Bankruptcy" title="Bankruptcy">bankruptcy</a> protection from creditors in the US as part of a recapitalisation and debt restructuring plan.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> On August 25, 2020 creditors approved the \xc2\xa31.2bn (\xe2\x82\xac1.3bn) rescue package and debt restructuring.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sir_Richard_Branson" class="mw-redirect" title="Sir Richard Branson">Sir Richard Branson</a> also injected 200 million pounds raised from the sale of shares in his <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Galactic" title="Virgin Galactic">Virgin Galactic</a> Holdings Inc. space venture.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On September 4, 2020, Virgin Atlantic announced a second round of job cuts, totalling 1,150 across all departments. Since the start of 2020, the company has halved its workforce due to the COVID-19 pandemic. Shai Weiss, chief executive of the company said "Further reducing the number of people we employ is heartbreaking but essential."<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Corporate_affairs">Corporate affairs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Virgin_Atlantic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Corporate affairs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Offices">Offices</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Virgin_Atlantic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Offices">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Virgin_Atlantic_HQ,_Manor_Royal,_Crawley.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Virgin_Atlantic_HQ%2C_Manor_Royal%2C_Crawley.JPG/220px-Virgin_Atlantic_HQ%2C_Manor_Royal%2C_Crawley.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Virgin_Atlantic_HQ%2C_Manor_Royal%2C_Crawley.JPG/330px-Virgin_Atlantic_HQ%2C_Manor_Royal%2C_Crawley.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Virgin_Atlantic_HQ%2C_Manor_Royal%2C_Crawley.JPG/440px-Virgin_Atlantic_HQ%2C_Manor_Royal%2C_Crawley.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Virgin_Atlantic_HQ,_Manor_Royal,_Crawley.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The former head office building <i>The Office</i> in <a href="/wiki/Crawley" title="Crawley">Crawley</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Virgin Atlantic\'s head office, known as <i>The VHQ</i>, is located on a business park in <a href="/wiki/Crawley" title="Crawley">Crawley</a>, <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a>, near <a href="/wiki/Gatwick_Airport" title="Gatwick Airport">Gatwick Airport</a><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> and also houses the corporate offices of <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Holidays" title="Virgin Holidays">Virgin Holidays</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> The company operates several offices and call centres around the United Kingdom, including a large office in <a href="/wiki/Swansea" title="Swansea">Swansea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wales" title="Wales">Wales</a>, which is a base for reservations, sales, baggage claims and tracing, \'live chat\' web support and a customer relations department.\n</p><p>International offices are located at <a href="/wiki/Atlanta,_Georgia" class="mw-redirect" title="Atlanta, Georgia">Atlanta</a>, Barbados, Greater Delhi, Hong Kong, Johannesburg, Lagos and Shanghai.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ownership">Ownership</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Virgin_Atlantic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Ownership">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Virgin Group sold a 49% stake in the airline to <a href="/wiki/Singapore_Airlines" title="Singapore Airlines">Singapore Airlines</a> in 1999 for \xc2\xa3600&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> On 14 May 2008, Singapore Airlines formally announced an invitation for offers for its Virgin Atlantic stake, and publicly acknowledged that its stake in the airline had "underperformed".<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In November 2010 it was reported that Virgin Atlantic had appointed <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Bank" title="Deutsche Bank">Deutsche Bank</a> to begin a strategic review of options for the airline following the tie-up between British Airways and American Airlines.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> By February 2011 it was confirmed that <a href="/wiki/SkyTeam" title="SkyTeam">SkyTeam</a> members <a href="/wiki/Air_France-KLM" class="mw-redirect" title="Air France-KLM">Air France-KLM</a> and Delta Air Lines had appointed <a href="/wiki/Goldman_Sachs" title="Goldman Sachs">Goldman Sachs</a> to advise them on a joint potential approach for Virgin Atlantic. <a href="/wiki/Etihad_Airways" title="Etihad Airways">Etihad Airways</a> was also reported to be considering a deal,<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Willie_Walsh_(Irish_businessman)" class="mw-redirect" title="Willie Walsh (Irish businessman)">Willie Walsh</a>, chief executive of <a href="/wiki/International_Airlines_Group" title="International Airlines Group">International Airlines Group</a>, stated that they would be interested in the airline, but only for the lucrative take-off and landing slots it holds at Heathrow Airport.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 11 December 2012, Delta Air Lines confirmed the purchase of Singapore Airlines\' 49% stake in Virgin Atlantic for \xc2\xa3224 million, with plans to develop a transatlantic joint venture. Regulatory approval from the United States and European Union was granted on 20 June 2013,<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> and the purchase was completed on 24 June.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> In December 2012, <a href="/wiki/International_Airlines_Group" title="International Airlines Group">International Airlines Group</a> CEO, Willie Walsh, suggested that the loss-making company would be history within five years. "I can\'t see Delta wanting to operate the Virgin brand because if they do what does that say about the Delta brand? I just don\'t see that the guy [Branson] has anything that stands out in terms of what he has achieved in the industry."<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In July 2017, Virgin Group agreed to sell a 31% stake in the airline to Air France-KLM for \xc2\xa3220 million, leaving it with a 20% holding.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> The deal fell through in late 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-FT_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FT-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Business_trends">Business trends</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Virgin_Atlantic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Business trends">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The key trends for Virgin Atlantic are shown below (from 2014 onwards, figures are for year ending December; earlier figures are for year ending February, and exclude <a href="/wiki/Air_Nigeria" title="Air Nigeria">Virgin Nigeria</a> operations 2005\xe2\x80\x932008):\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable" style="margin: 1em auto; id="cite_ref-Virgin_Atlantic_press_information_66-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Virgin_Atlantic_press_information-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td><sup id="cite_ref-UK_CAA_65-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UK_CAA-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Virgin_Atlantic_press_information_66-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Virgin_Atlantic_press_information-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td><sup id="cite_ref-UK_CAA_65-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UK_CAA-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Virgin_Atlantic_press_information_66-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Virgin_Atlantic_press_information-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td><sup id="cite_ref-Virgin_Atlantic_press_information_66-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Virgin_Atlantic_press_information-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup><br /><sup id="cite_ref-2012results_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2012results-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2013sust_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2013sust-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td><sup id="cite_ref-2013_Results_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2013_Results-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Financial_Times_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Financial_Times-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td><sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td><sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td><sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td><sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td><sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Service_concept">Service concept</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Virgin_Atlantic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Service concept">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Virgin_lounge,_Heathrow.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Virgin_lounge%2C_Heathrow.jpg/220px-Virgin_lounge%2C_Heathrow.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Virgin_lounge%2C_Heathrow.jpg/330px-Virgin_lounge%2C_Heathrow.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Virgin_lounge%2C_Heathrow.jpg/440px-Virgin_lounge%2C_Heathrow.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Virgin_lounge,_Heathrow.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>Clubhouse</i> lounge at <a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Airport" title="Heathrow Airport">Heathrow Airport</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Virgin Atlantic aircraft operate with a three-class cabin configuration: <a href="/wiki/Economy_Class" class="mw-redirect" title="Economy Class">Economy</a>, Premium (formerly <a href="/wiki/Premium_Economy" class="mw-redirect" title="Premium Economy">Premium economy</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-:0_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> and Upper Class - the <a href="/wiki/Business_class" title="Business class">business class</a> product. Premium has a separate check-in area, priority boarding and a wider seat with more legroom. Upper Class features a seat that converts into a fully flat bed and access to chauffeur drive(in a private check in area called the Upper Class Wing at London Heathrow).<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> Virgin Atlantic was the first airline to offer personal entertainment for all passengers in all classes.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>Interestingly, the airline has shown films in the past which included plane crashes.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The airline\'s <a href="/wiki/Frequent-flyer_program" title="Frequent-flyer program">frequent-flyer program</a> is styled \'the Flying Club\'.\n</p><p>Virgin Atlantic operates 6 <a href="/wiki/Airport_lounge" title="Airport lounge">lounges</a> worldwide called \'Clubhouse\' at London Heathrow, New York-JFK, Boston, Washington D.C.-Dulles, San Francisco and Johannesburg.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> It also operates a \'Revivals\' arrival lounge in London Heathrow. They are accessible for passengers travelling in Upper Class and Flying Club Gold tier members. Where applicable, Upper Class passengers are also welcome to use Delta Sky Clubs prior to departure.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Little_Red">Little Red</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Virgin_Atlantic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Little Red">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Atlantic_Little_Red" title="Virgin Atlantic Little Red">Virgin Atlantic Little Red</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Virgin_Atlantic_Airbus_A320-214;_EI-EZW@LHR;13.05.2013_708fk_(8738115862).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Virgin_Atlantic_Airbus_A320-214%3B_EI-EZW%40LHR%3B13.05.2013_708fk_%288738115862%29.jpg/220px-Virgin_Atlantic_Airbus_A320-214%3B_EI-EZW%40LHR%3B13.05.2013_708fk_%288738115862%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Virgin_Atlantic_Airbus_A320-214%3B_EI-EZW%40LHR%3B13.05.2013_708fk_%288738115862%29.jpg/330px-Virgin_Atlantic_Airbus_A320-214%3B_EI-EZW%40LHR%3B13.05.2013_708fk_%288738115862%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Virgin_Atlantic_Airbus_A320-214%3B_EI-EZW%40LHR%3B13.05.2013_708fk_%288738115862%29.jpg/440px-Virgin_Atlantic_Airbus_A320-214%3B_EI-EZW%40LHR%3B13.05.2013_708fk_%288738115862%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3363" data-file-height="2234" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Virgin_Atlantic_Airbus_A320-214;_EI-EZW@LHR;13.05.2013_708fk_(8738115862).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Virgin Atlantic <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A320-200" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus A320-200">Airbus A320-200</a> <i>Little Red</i> operated by Aer Lingus</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/British_Midland_International" title="British Midland International">British Midland International</a> provided domestic and European feeder traffic into Heathrow Airport in partnership with Virgin<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> until it was purchased by British Airways\' parent company <a href="/wiki/International_Airlines_Group" title="International Airlines Group">International Airlines Group</a> in 2011. The <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa" title="Lufthansa">Lufthansa</a>-owned airline had faced heavy annual losses of more than \xc2\xa3100 million. Under the terms of the takeover, IAG had to relinquish some former BMI domestic slots at Heathrow. Virgin Atlantic purchased enough slots in 2012 to enable it to launch a domestic service on 31 March 2013, under the Little Red brand, operating a total of 12 daily services from London to <a href="/wiki/Aberdeen_Airport" title="Aberdeen Airport">Aberdeen</a> (three), <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh_Airport" title="Edinburgh Airport">Edinburgh</a> (six), and Manchester (three).<sup id="cite_ref-Domestic_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Domestic-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> The airline <a href="/wiki/Aircraft_lease" title="Aircraft lease">wet-leased</a> four Airbus <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A320-200" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus A320-200">Airbus A320-200s</a> from <a href="/wiki/Aer_Lingus" title="Aer Lingus">Aer Lingus</a>, operating with Virgin Atlantic livery, under a three-year contract.<sup id="cite_ref-Lingus_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lingus-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In September 2014, it was reported that Virgin Atlantic was considering closing its domestic brand after suffering heavy losses,<sup id="cite_ref-Little_Red_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Little_Red-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> with <a href="/wiki/Civil_Aviation_Authority_(United_Kingdom)" title="Civil Aviation Authority (United Kingdom)">Civil Aviation Authority</a> figures confirming an average seat occupancy level of just 37.6% in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-telegraph_little_red_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-telegraph_little_red-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> The 12 daily pairs of take-off and landing slots at Heathrow cannot be sold to be used for long-haul routes.<sup id="cite_ref-BMIslots_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BMIslots-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 6 October 2014, Virgin Atlantic confirmed that the Little Red service would cease; flights to Manchester ended on 28 March 2015 and flights to Edinburgh and Aberdeen ended on 26 September 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Virgin_Atlantic_International_Limited">Virgin Atlantic International Limited</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Virgin_Atlantic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Virgin Atlantic International Limited">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>On 13 April 2015, Virgin Atlantic incorporated a new subsidiary \xe2\x80\x93 Virgin Atlantic International Limited (VAIL).<sup id="cite_ref-VAIcompany_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VAIcompany-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> In November 2015, VAIL obtained its own <a href="/wiki/Air_operator%27s_certificate" title="Air operator&#39;s certificate">Air Operators Certificate</a> and Operating Licence, and commenced operations with two former Virgin Atlantic Airways Limited operated <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A330-300" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus A330-300">Airbus A330-300</a> aircraft taking over routes previously operated by Virgin Atlantic Limited between London Gatwick and Barbados, St Lucia, Antigua, Grenada and Tobago.<sup id="cite_ref-VAIL_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VAIL-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> These flights are operated on behalf of Virgin Atlantic.<sup id="cite_ref-VAIL2_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VAIL2-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Upon incorporation as an AOC holder, the majority of Virgin Atlantic\'s landing slots at London Heathrow Airport were transferred to VAIL, allowing Virgin Atlantic to access the value of the carriers\' slots by \'<a href="/wiki/Mortgage_loan" title="Mortgage loan">mortgaging</a>\' them through open investment from capital markets, the first time in Europe a company has used airport take-off and landing slots to generate money in this way.<sup id="cite_ref-Slots_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Slots-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Slots2_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Slots2-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Flybe_takeover_bid">Flybe takeover bid</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Virgin_Atlantic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Flybe takeover bid">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>On 11 January 2019, Virgin Atlantic formed the <a href="/wiki/Connect_Airways" title="Connect Airways">Connect Airways</a> consortium with <a href="/wiki/Stobart_Group#Stobart_Aviation" class="mw-redirect" title="Stobart Group">Stobart Aviation</a> and Cyrus Capital, to make a takeover bid for <a href="/wiki/Flybe" title="Flybe">Flybe</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-fg-20190111_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fg-20190111-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-fg-20190111-cuts_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fg-20190111-cuts-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> The deal would see the consortium combine Flybe and <a href="/wiki/Stobart_Air" title="Stobart Air">Stobart Air</a> with Virgin Atlantic to create an integrated carrier operating under the Virgin Atlantic brand.<sup id="cite_ref-insidermedia-20190111_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-insidermedia-20190111-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> Flybe and Stobart Air would however retain their own <a href="/wiki/Air_Operator_Certificate" class="mw-redirect" title="Air Operator Certificate">Air Operator Certificates</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> On 15 January 2019, Connect Airways announced an increased offer, which Flybe\'s board accepted.<sup id="cite_ref-atwonline-20190115_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-atwonline-20190115-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> On 21 February 2019, the Flybe Group confirmed that its operating assets, including the airline and the website, had indeed been transferred to Connect Airways, despite a last-minute rival bid.<sup id="cite_ref-cityam-20190221_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cityam-20190221-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> However, despite the investment of \xc2\xa3135 million from Connect Airways into Flybe, the airline filed for administration and ceased operations with immediate effect in March 2020, following reduced demand that Virgin Atlantic attributed to the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a> and the UK government failing to grant a \xc2\xa3100 million loan.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Flybecollapse_41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Flybecollapse-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Destinations">Destinations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Virgin_Atlantic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Destinations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Virgin_Atlantic_destinations" title="List of Virgin Atlantic destinations">List of Virgin Atlantic destinations</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Virgin_Atlantic_Destinations.svg" color:black;">&#160;</span>&#160;Terminated</div></div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Codeshare_agreements">Codeshare agreements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Virgin_Atlantic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Codeshare agreements">edit</a><span 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Virgin_Atlantic%2C_G-VNEW_Boeing_787_Dreamliner_%2816901493414%29.jpg/400px-Virgin_Atlantic%2C_G-VNEW_Boeing_787_Dreamliner_%2816901493414%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4446" data-file-height="2365" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption">Virgin Atlantic <a href="/wiki/Boeing_787_Dreamliner" title="Boeing 787 Dreamliner">Boeing 787-9</a></div></div></div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Current_fleet">Current fleet</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Virgin_Atlantic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Current fleet">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Virgin Atlantic Airways Ltd. operates an all-widebody fleet. It consists of the following aircraft as of September&#160;2020<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Virgin_Atlantic&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>:<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-vsfleetpage_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vsfleetpage-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<center>\n<table class="wikitable" style="border-collapse:collapse;text-align:center">\n<caption>Virgin Atlantic fleet\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<th rowspan="2">Aircraft\n</th>\n<th rowspan="2">In <br A330-900</a></span>\n</td>\n<td>&#8212;\n</td>\n<td>14\n</td>\n<td colspan="5"><abbr title="To be announced">TBA</abbr>\n</td>\n<td>Order with 6 options.<br />Deliveries planned to begin 2022<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Airbus_A350-1000" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus A350-1000">Airbus A350-1000</a>\n</td>\n<td>7\n</td>\n<td>5\n</td>\n<td>44\n</td>\n<td>56\n</td>\n<td>235\n</td>\n<td>335\n</td>\n<td><sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Boeing_787-9" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 787-9">Boeing 787-9</a>\n</td>\n<td>17\n</td>\n<td>&#8212;\n</td>\n<td>31\n</td>\n<td>35\n</td>\n<td>198\n</td>\n<td>264\n</td>\n<td><sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th>Total\n</th>\n<th>37\n</th>\n<th>19\n</th>\n<th colspan="6">\n</th></tr></tbody></table>\n</center>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fleet_development">Fleet development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Virgin_Atlantic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Fleet development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Virgin Atlantic has a mixed fleet of twin-engined <a href="/wiki/Airbus" title="Airbus">Airbus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Boeing_Commercial_Airplanes" title="Boeing Commercial Airplanes">Boeing</a> widebody aircraft. As a result of COVID-19 restructuring, the airline\'s fleet of <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A330-200" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus A330-200">Airbus A330-200s</a>, <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A330" title="Airbus A330">A330-300s</a>, <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A350_XWB" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus A350 XWB">A350-1000s</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Boeing_787_Dreamliner" title="Boeing 787 Dreamliner">Boeing 787-9s</a> will operate interchangeably on routes to all destinations from London\'s <a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Airport" title="Heathrow Airport">Heathrow Airport</a>, and from <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Airport" title="Manchester Airport">Manchester airport</a> to the United States, Pakistan and the Caribbean. Seasonal routes to <a href="/wiki/Orlando_International_Airport" title="Orlando International Airport">Orlando International Airport</a>, from <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Airport" title="Glasgow Airport">Glasgow</a> and <a href="/wiki/Belfast_International_Airport" title="Belfast International Airport">Belfast International Airport</a> have been postponed until the 2021 summer season due to the COVID-19 pandemic. The aircraft that will be operating the seasonal routes next year will be the <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A330" title="Airbus A330">A330-300s</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In August 2002, Virgin Atlantic became the first airline to operate the <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A340-600" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus A340-600">Airbus A340-600</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 27 September 2006, <a href="/wiki/Richard_Branson" title="Richard Branson">Richard Branson</a> announced plans to reduce <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas_emissions" title="Greenhouse gas emissions">greenhouse gas emissions</a> by cutting aircraft weight and fuel consumption. There was also an experiment in 2007 in partnership with Boeing to have aircraft towed to the runway to save fuel, as a potential change to future operational procedures.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> Virgin Atlantic also volunteered a Boeing 747 for a test of <a href="/wiki/Biofuels" class="mw-redirect" title="Biofuels">biofuels</a> in February 2008. The aircraft flew without passengers from Heathrow to <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Airport_Schiphol" title="Amsterdam Airport Schiphol">Amsterdam Airport Schiphol</a>, with 20% of the power for one engine provided by plant-based biofuel. Virgin Atlantic said that it expected to use <a href="/wiki/Algae" title="Algae">algae</a>-based biofuels in the future.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Virgin Atlantic took delivery of its first <a href="/wiki/Boeing_787-9" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 787-9">Boeing 787-9</a> in October 2014, becoming the first European airline to fly the variant.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> Virgin Atlantic\'s order was first announced on 24 April 2007, and is for a total of 17 aircraft, with <a href="/wiki/Option_(aircraft_purchasing)" title="Option (aircraft purchasing)">options</a> on five more. The exercised options will replace the Heathrow-based 747 fleet during 2015 and 2016. Virgin Atlantic had also ordered six <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A380-800" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus A380-800">Airbus A380-800</a> aircraft, with options on a further six, delivery initially due in 2006. This order was officially cancelled in March 2018, with deposits transferred to A330 and A350 aircraft orders.\n</p><p>The older Airbus A340-300 aircraft were withdrawn from service in April 2015, as rising costs had made it less economical to run the type. Virgin Atlantic had begun to replace the A340-300 on routes with the two-engine A330-300 and 787-9. The final Virgin Atlantic A340-300 flight was made on 9 April, landing at Heathrow early on 10 April.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> Eight A340-600s remained in service.\n</p><p>The airline\'s A330s, in three-class layout, have been stationed at Heathrow Airport since April 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Branson announced in March 2016 that <a href="/wiki/The_Spaceship_Company" title="The Spaceship Company">The Spaceship Company</a> would partner with <a href="/wiki/Boom_Technology" title="Boom Technology">Boom Technology</a> to develop supersonic jets capable of travelling between London and New York in three and a half hours. He confirmed that Virgin Atlantic had options on 10 of the aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-boom20160323_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-boom20160323-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In July 2016, Virgin Atlantic announced an order for 12 <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A350_XWB" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus A350 XWB">Airbus A350-1000</a> aircraft, to eventually replace the ageing four-engined <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747-400" title="Boeing 747-400">Boeing 747-400</a> and <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A340" title="Airbus A340">Airbus A340-600</a> fleets. The order consists of eight aircraft which will be purchased directly from <a href="/wiki/Airbus" title="Airbus">Airbus</a>, with a further four acquired through leasing companies. It is expected that the 12 A350-1000s on order will be split into two separate configurations, a business-oriented, premium heavy configuration, and leisure-oriented, economy heavy configuration for select routes to the Caribbean, Las Vegas, and Orlando, Florida. This order will leave Virgin Atlantic with a streamlined fleet of Airbus A330s, A350s and Boeing 787 aircraft, leaving just two pilot pools and increasing cost efficiencies.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> The A350s feature three classes&#160;&#8211;&#32;Economy (in a 3\xe2\x80\x933\xe2\x80\x933 layout), Premium (2\xe2\x80\x934\xe2\x80\x932) and Upper Class (1\xe2\x80\x932\xe2\x80\x931)&#160;&#8211;&#32; and a bar area known as <i>The Loft</i>, and was first introduced on the London to New York route in summer 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Due to engine fan-blade corrosion issues with the fleet of <a href="/wiki/Boeing_787_Dreamliner" title="Boeing 787 Dreamliner">Boeing 787</a> aircraft, Virgin Atlantic chose to move some of its <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Airport" title="Manchester Airport">Manchester</a>-based Boeing 747 and Airbus A330 aircraft to cover routes out of London Heathrow. In 2016, a spokesman for Rolls-Royce which manufacturers the Trent 1000s said the company "would start producing new corrosion-resistant fan blades by the start of 2017". Virgin Atlantic has had to temporarily park some of its 787s while they wait for attention. In place of these aircraft Virgin Atlantic has chosen to lease four former <a href="/wiki/Air_Berlin" title="Air Berlin">Air Berlin</a> A330-200 aircraft, which will be based in Manchester. The A330-200 aircraft arrived in 2018, with full Virgin Atlantic liveries, but with former Air Berlin cabin products, with Virgin Atlantic\'s Premium Economy to be retrofitted at a later date. Virgin Atlantic said it would add "resilience" to its fleet after the engine issues with its 787s. It was thought these aircraft would be on initial 12-month leases, allowing them to assess their viability in the fleet, with the possibility of extending the leases further.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> The airline also chose to reinstate a former A340-600 aircraft G-VNAP into the fleet from storage, after purchase from its lessor, to cover for one A340 aircraft leaving the fleet, for which the lease was unable to be extended.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In March 2018, <a href="/wiki/Airbus" title="Airbus">Airbus</a> announced the cancellation of Virgin Atlantic\'s order for six <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A380-800" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus A380-800">Airbus A380-800s</a> which it had placed back in 2001 and deferred several times since.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>At the 2019 <a href="/wiki/Paris_Air_Show" title="Paris Air Show">Paris Air Show</a> the airline signed a deal for up to 20 <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A330neo" title="Airbus A330neo">Airbus A330-900</a> aircraft making it the first UK customer for the aircraft. Eight aircraft are purchased directly from Airbus, six through <a href="/wiki/Air_Lease_Corporation" title="Air Lease Corporation">Air Lease Corporation</a>, and the airline has options on a further six aircraft. They will replace older Airbus A330-200s and -300s<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> with deliveries expected from September 2021 to 2024.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In July 2019, Virgin Atlantic initially announced the retirement of its remaining <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A340-600" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus A340-600">Airbus A340-600s</a> by November 2019, however in September 2019 had extended the A340-600\'s service to December 2019, while the airline\'s Boeing 787 aircraft undergo further repairs on their Rolls-Royce Trent 1000 engines.<sup id="cite_ref-ch-aviation.com_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ch-aviation.com-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> The retirement date for the A340-600 was subsequently postponed after several changes in date to May 2020, before the type was ultimately retired early on 9 March 2020, with the final scheduled A340-600 service taking place the day prior from Lagos to London Heathrow.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-A3402020_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A3402020-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-A340520_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A340520-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-A340retirement_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A340retirement-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The carrier took delivery of its first <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A350-1000" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus A350-1000">Airbus A350-1000</a> aircraft in August 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Virgin Atlantic announced the early retirement of the seven remaining <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747-400" title="Boeing 747-400">Boeing 747-400</a> aircraft on 5 May 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-747r_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-747r-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In December 2020, Virgin Atlantic sold and leased back two of their latest <a href="/wiki/Boeing_787_Dreamliner" title="Boeing 787 Dreamliner">Boeing 787-9</a> aircraft to fund the repayment of a loan from Griffin Global Asset Management and to raise up to \xc2\xa370 million ($93 million) worth of funds.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline"
