A340-300</a>\n</td>\n<td>10\n</td>\n<td>1993\n</td>\n<td>2015\n</td>\n<td>Last commercial flight 9 April 2015\n</td>\n<td>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Airbus_A340-600" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus A340-600">Airbus A340-600</a>\n</td>\n<td>19\n</td>\n<td>2002\n</td>\n<td>2020\n</td>\n<td>Launch customer; Last commercial flight 8 March 2020; G-VNAP in \'Thank You\' livery\n</td>\n<td align="center"><sup id="cite_ref-A340retirement_135-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A340retirement-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Boeing_747-100" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 747-100">Boeing 747-100</a>\n</td>\n<td>1\n</td>\n<td>1990\n</td>\n<td>2000\n</td>\n<td>G-VMIA named <i>Spirit of Sir Freddie</i> after Sir <a href="/wiki/Freddie_Laker" title="Freddie Laker">Freddie Laker</a>\n</td>\n<td>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Boeing_747-200B" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 747-200B">Boeing 747-200B</a>\n</td>\n<td>16\n</td>\n<td>1984\n</td>\n<td>2005\n</td>\n<td>G-VIRG was Virgin Atlantic\'s first aircraft\n</td>\n<td>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Boeing_747-400" title="Boeing 747-400">Boeing 747-400</a>\n</td>\n<td>13\n</td>\n<td>1994\n</td>\n<td>2020\n</td>\n<td>Last commercial flight 5 May 2020<br />Retired early due to the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><sup id="cite_ref-747r_137-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-747r-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Boeing_767-300ER" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 767-300ER">Boeing 767-300ER</a>\n</td>\n<td>1\n</td>\n<td>1996\n</td>\n<td>1997\n</td>\n<td>Leased from <a href="/wiki/Martinair" title="Martinair">Martinair</a>\n</td>\n<td>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n</center>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Livery">Livery</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Virgin_Atlantic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Livery">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:G-VFAB_Boeing_747-400_Virgin_Atlantic_(14622727959).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/G-VFAB_Boeing_747-400_Virgin_Atlantic_%2814622727959%29.jpg/220px-G-VFAB_Boeing_747-400_Virgin_Atlantic_%2814622727959%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/G-VFAB_Boeing_747-400_Virgin_Atlantic_%2814622727959%29.jpg/330px-G-VFAB_Boeing_747-400_Virgin_Atlantic_%2814622727959%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/G-VFAB_Boeing_747-400_Virgin_Atlantic_%2814622727959%29.jpg/440px-G-VFAB_Boeing_747-400_Virgin_Atlantic_%2814622727959%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="683" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:G-VFAB_Boeing_747-400_Virgin_Atlantic_(14622727959).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Boeing_747-400" title="Boeing 747-400">Boeing 747-400</a> <i>Lady Penelope</i> in <i>Birthday Girl</i> livery in 2014, on approach to <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport" title="John F. Kennedy International Airport">New York-JFK</a>, NY, United States</div></div></div>\n<p>Virgin Atlantic\'s first aircraft were painted with a <a href="/wiki/Aircraft_livery#Eurowhite" title="Aircraft livery">"Eurowhite"</a> design with a red stripe through the centre of the main deck windows. The engines were metallic silver and the tail red with the logo in white. In the 1990s, the refreshed design was introduced, removing the centre red stripe through the windows, engines were painted red, the Virgin Atlantic titles in grey were added along the main fuselage, and the \'Flying Lady\' was introduced to the nose area.\n</p><p>In October 2006, with the delivery of G-VRED, Virgin Atlantic introduced a new design, with the fuselage painted in metallic silver and a revised tail fin, with red and purple features and the logo. Near the nose of each aircraft is a <a href="/wiki/Pin-up_girl" class="mw-redirect" title="Pin-up girl">pin-up girl</a>, the "Scarlet Lady", carrying a Union flag, which was designed by British artist Ken White, who modelled the motif on the World War II pin-ups of <a href="/wiki/Alberto_Vargas" title="Alberto Vargas">Alberto Vargas</a> \xe2\x80\x93 hence the naming one of the fleet <i>Varga Girl</i> (in this case, an A340-600 registered G-VGAS).<sup id="cite_ref-Virgin_Atlantic_press_information_66-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Virgin_Atlantic_press_information-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Each aircraft has a name, usually feminine, such as <i>Ladybird</i>, <i>Island Lady</i>, and <i>Ruby Tuesday</i>, but some are linked to registrations (e.g. G-VFIZ became <i>Bubbles</i>). A couple are commemorative names (e.g. G-VEIL\xe2\x80\x94<i>Queen of the Skies</i>\xe2\x80\x94which was named by <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Queen Elizabeth II</a> on 7 April 2004, marking the centenary of the <a href="/wiki/Entente_Cordiale" title="Entente Cordiale">Entente Cordiale</a>; this frame exited the fleet in April 2016). An exception is <i>Spirit of Sir Freddie</i>. An early Boeing 747, it was named in honour of <a href="/wiki/Freddie_Laker" title="Freddie Laker">Freddie Laker</a> of Laker Airways, who helped Virgin Atlantic following the demise of his own airline. G-VFAB\xe2\x80\x94<i>Lady Penelope</i>\xe2\x80\x94gained a special livery to celebrate Virgin Atlantic\'s 21st birthday. G-VFAB, <i>Lady Penelope</i>, exited the fleet in September 2015 after 21 years of service and was subsequently parted out.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> In 2018 Virgin Atlantic unveiled a special edition "thank you" livery dedicated to its 9.000 staff worldwide on the now-retired G-VNAP.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>However, not all names are decided by the company. In 2006 Virgin Atlantic ran an eBay auction to name one of their Airbus A340-600 aircraft, registered G-VYOU, for a year. The winning bid was for \xc2\xa310,000, and the winner named the aircraft \'Emmeline Heaney\' after his newborn daughter. The name adorned the aircraft for the remainder of its operating service until the aircraft was retired in October 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The current livery dates from 2010 and returns to the "Eurowhite" design featuring purple billboard titles on the fuselage, slight changes to the Scarlet Lady, and new red metallic paint for the aircraft\'s tail and engines. On aircraft that have winglets, the wingtips are red, with the logo on the inside facing passengers on board. The Virgin Atlantic logo was also added in purple billboard titles to the underside of the aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> The former livery with black billboard titles and flying lady still remain on some older aircraft.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Incidents_and_accidents">Incidents and accidents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Virgin_Atlantic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Incidents and accidents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Virgin Atlantic is considered to have a strong safety reputation. Since the airline\'s founding in 1984, it has never suffered a complete hull-loss incident or a passenger fatality.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li>On 5 November 1997, after numerous attempts to shake free the jammed main landing gear of an <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A340-300" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus A340-300">Airbus A340-300</a> (G-VSKY) failed, the aircraft en route from Los Angeles to Heathrow made an emergency landing at Heathrow Airport. The aircraft sustained major damage to the undersides of engines one, two, and four, which made contact with the runway surface during landing. The runway surface was also damaged and several runway lights were broken as the right main landing gear wheels broke up during the deceleration. The aircraft was evacuated safely. Two crew members and five passengers sustained minor injuries during the evacuation.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> The damaged aircraft was repaired after the incident and was retired from the Virgin Atlantic fleet in 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>On 8 February 2005, on board an <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A340-600" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus A340-600">Airbus A340-600</a> aircraft (G-VATL) en route from Hong Kong to Heathrow, the fuel control computer system caused a loss of automatic fuel transfer between tanks. The left outboard engine lost power, and shortly afterwards the right outboard engine also began to falter until the crew began to crossfeed fuel manually. The pilots diverted to Amsterdam and landed safely. The interim accident report made four safety recommendations addressed to the primary certification bodies for large transport category aircraft (<a href="/wiki/European_Aviation_Safety_Agency" title="European Aviation Safety Agency">EASA</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Aviation_Administration" title="Federal Aviation Administration">FAA</a>), advising on the need for a low-fuel warning system for large aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>On 15 March 2021, Virgin Atlantic flight 453 operated by a <a href="/wiki/Boeing_787-9" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 787-9">Boeing 787-9</a> en route to Tel Aviv from Heathrow was forced to return to Heathrow whilst flying over Paris after the aircraft was subject to a laser attack from the ground. The flight crew issued an emergency <i>Pan</i> call after the captain lost sight in one eye and was unable to fly the 787. No other injuries were reported.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Virgin_Atlantic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: See
